## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard dependent variable in kinetic rate laws for batch/closed systems. With only t and A available, the most likely structures are reaction-order rate laws and time-varying effective rate coefficients (e.g., catalyst deactivation, changing conditions, external forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or saturated regime)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant source term, e.g., feed or generation at constant rate)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition analogue)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction with both reactants ∝ A)
- General nth-order law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fit)
- Parallel first+second order loss: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (two competing loss pathways)
- Source–sink (linear relaxation): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production plus first-order removal; approach to steady state)
- Reversible/pseudo-first-order with background term: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (back-reaction effectively constant, or reservoir coupling)
- Autocatalytic growth with depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating early behavior with finite capacity/depletion)
- Inhibited/limited-rate decay (self-inhibition): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + 1) (rate suppressed at high A due to inhibition/crowding)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions causing k(t) to drift)
- Catalyst/activity deactivation: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate decreases exponentially in time)
- Activation/induction period: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps up from ~0 to steady value)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-periodic effective rate constant)
- Empirical mixed time–concentration coupling: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (order-law with time-decaying activity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Overall sign: if A is a reactant being consumed, dA_dt is typically negative and often proportional to a nonnegative function of A.
- Reaction order identification: log(-dA_dt) linear in log(A) suggests power-law form -c0*A**c1; curvature indicates mixed orders (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2).
- Presence of a constant term (±c0) implies external source/sink, background formation, or coupling to a large reservoir rather than closed-system decay.
- Time-varying coefficients k(t) multiplying A (e.g., (c0+c1*t)*A or exp(-c*t)*A) indicate changing conditions such as catalyst deactivation, temperature drift, or aging.
- Rational forms like -c0*A/(c1*A+1) indicate inhibition, limited accessibility, or transport/coverage limitations that reduce apparent rate at high A.
- Autocatalytic structure A*(c1-A) implies slow start (near-zero rate at low A), acceleration at intermediate A, and slowdown near a limiting concentration (resource limitation/depletion).
- Sinusoidal dependence on t indicates externally driven periodic modulation (light intensity cycles, pulsed feeding, mixing/flow oscillations).
- If dA_dt approaches 0 as t increases while A remains nonzero, a decaying prefactor in t (e.g., exp(-c*t)) is a strong candidate (loss of activity rather than depletion).
- If A tends to a nonzero steady state A* where dA_dt=0, linear source–sink (c0-c1*A) or reversible-like (-c0*A+c1) structures are natural candidates.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. `-0.16498*A²` (polynomial in A)
2. `-0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t)` (A times exponential in t)
3. `0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))` (sine of log of (A+1))

The key distinguishing feature is the `sin(log(A+1))` term. This is a very specific basis function that cannot be replicated by polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, or simple logarithms.

Let me check which candidates contain `sin(log(...))`:

- **Candidate 30:** `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(Ac7+1) + c8)` — Has `sin(log(...))` ✓
- **Candidate 55:** `Ac0 + Ac1*exp(c2*t) + A^c3*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(Ac8+1) + c9)` — Has `sin(log(...))` ✓
- **Candidate 54:** Has `cos(log(...))` which equals `sin(log(...) + π/2)`, but no sin term directly.

Let me analyze these carefully:

**Candidate 30:** `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(Ac7+1) + c8)`
- Set c0 = -0.16498, c1 = 0, c2 = -0.16498, c3 = -0.01276, c4 = 0, c5 = 0.6208, c6 = 1, c7 = 1, c8 = 0
- This gives: `-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A+1))` ✓ **MATCH**

**Candidate 55:** `Ac0 + Ac1*exp(c2*t) + A^c3*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(Ac8+1) + c9)`
- Need A² term: set c3 = 2, c4 = -0.16498 → A²*(-0.16498)
- Set c0 = 0, c1 = -0.16498, c2 = -0.01276, c5 = 0, c6 = 0.6208, c7 = 1, c8 = 1, c9 = 0
- This gives: `-0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) - 0.16498*A² + 0.6208*sin(log(A+1))` ✓ **MATCH**

**Candidate 54:** `Ac0 + Ac1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(Ac4+1) + c5 + c6*cos(c7*log(Ac8+1))`
- cos can be written as sin with phase shift, but we need sin(log(A+1)) and this has cos(c7*log(Ac8+1)). However, cos(x) = sin(x + π/2), so cos(log(A+1)) = sin(log(A+1) + π/2) ≠ sin(log(A+1)). We'd need cos(log(A+1) - π/2) = sin(log(A+1)), but there's no phase shift parameter in the cos. Also missing A² term (no A^c power term). **NO MATCH**

Let me verify no other candidates have trigonometric functions: Candidate 10 has cos(c9*t) (not log), Candidate 45 has log|t|. None others have sin/cos of log.
